Definition of the Natural Body
Al-Mawaqif defines the natural body and explains the right angle and method of imagining dimensions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Islamic theologians (mutakallimun) define the natural body in terms of the possibility of imagining three mutually perpendicular dimensions.

Core Idea
The natural body is defined by the possibility of three perpendicular extensions, not by actual dimensions.

This lesson explores the classical kalam definition of the natural body. Al-Mawaqif begins by establishing what a body is at its most fundamental level: a substance (jawhar) that admits three-dimensional extension. The definition is based on what can be imagined, not on what is physically present, which sets the stage for later discussions on atomism and space.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic definition carefully
Read the first sentence of the passage slowly. Notice the key terms: الجوهر (substance) and الامتداد (extension). Understand that the definition hinges on the possibility (can be assumed) rather than actual existence.
2
Understand the right angle explanation
The second part defines a right angle (الزاوية القائمة) as the angle formed when a line stands perpendicular on another, creating two equal angles. This geometric clarification is necessary to understand the mutual perpendicularity of the three dimensions.
3
Visualize the three dimensions
The third part gives a method for assuming length, width, and depth. Notice the sequence: first length arbitrarily, then width perpendicular to it, then depth uniquely determined. This shows that the three dimensions are not all arbitrary.
The depth is determined once length and width are chosen.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الجسم الطبيعي هو الجوهر الذي يمكن أن يفرض فيه امتداد وامتداد آخر مقاطع على قوائم وامتداد ثالث مقاطع لهما على جميع قوائم. ومعنى الزاوية القائمة أنه إذا قام خط على خط عموداً عليه لا ميل له إلى أحد الطرفين أصلاً، حتى حدثت من جنبتيه زاويتان متساويتان فكل واحدة منهما قائمة. وتصوير فرض الأبعاد الثلاثة المتقاطعة في الجسم أن نفرض فيه بعداً ما كيف اتفق أي لا يتعين لفرضه جهة وهو الطول ثم نفرض بعداً آخر في أي جهة شئناً من الجهتين الباقيتين مقاطعاً له بقائمة وهو العرض ثم نفرض بعداً ثالثاً مقاطعاً لهما بحيث يحصل منه بالنسبة إلى كل من الأولين أربع قوائم أي على زوايا قائمة وهذا البعد الثالث متعين لا يتصور غير واحد.
The natural body is the substance in which can be assumed an extension and another extension intersecting at right angles, and a third extension intersecting both at all right angles. The meaning of a right angle is that when a line stands on a line perpendicular to it with no inclination to either side at all, so that two equal angles arise from its two sides, each of them is a right angle. The depiction of the assumption of the three intersecting dimensions in a body is that we assume in it a dimension arbitrarily, i.e., its direction is not determined, and it is the length; then we assume another dimension in any direction we wish from the remaining two directions intersecting it at a right angle, and it is the width; then we assume a third dimension intersecting both such that from it with respect to each of the first two there are four right angles, i.e., at right angles, and this third dimension is determined, only one being conceivable.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage begins by defining the natural body (al-jism al-ṭabīʿī) as a substance (jawhar) in which three mutually perpendicular extensions can be imagined. The definition emphasizes possibility (imkān), not actual existence. Then it explains the nature of a right angle (al-zāwiya al-qāʾima): when one line stands perpendicular on another, two equal angles are formed, each being a right angle. Finally, it describes a method for imagining the three dimensions: first assume a direction (length), then a second perpendicular to it (width), then a third perpendicular to both (depth/height), which is uniquely determined. The author follows the logical order of the definition, clarifying each component.

Key Terms

الزاوية القائمة
الأبعاد الثلاثة
جوهر
امتداد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A body must have actual three-dimensional extension to be a body.
Correction: The definition only requires the possibility of assuming three mutually perpendicular dimensions, not actual existence.

Checkpoint
According to the definition, what is a natural body?
A) A substance that possesses actual three dimensions.
B) A substance in which three mutually perpendicular dimensions can be assumed.
C) A substance that has length, width, and depth in reality.
D) A substance that is infinitely extended.

Key Takeaway
The natural body is defined by the possibility of imagining three mutually perpendicular dimensions, not by its actual physical extension.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that a body is defined by the possibility of three perpendicular extensions, not by its actual size. When you look at the physical objects you own—your phone, your car, your home—do you see them as mere 'possibilities' in your perception? How attached are you to their actuality? Will you remember today that their physical reality is ultimately contingent upon Allah's creation?
?
The third dimension is uniquely determined once the first two are set. In your life, are there choices that uniquely determine your path? Are you living as if your decisions have no consequences, or do you recognize that every step after repentance determines a unique path back to Allah?
?
The definition focuses on possibility (imkān) rather than actuality. What 'actual' things in your life are you holding too tightly, forgetting that they are only possible by Allah's permission? How can you turn that attachment into gratitude and reliance on the Creator of all dimensions?

The Right-Angle Condition in the Definition of Body
Author defines body and explains why the right-angle condition is needed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the condition of right-angle intersection is included in the definition of body, and how it relates to the quiddity of body and the distinction from surface.

Core Idea
The right-angle condition defines body's quiddity, not its distinction from surface.

In defining body, scholars include the condition that the three dimensions intersect at right angles. But why is this condition necessary? In this passage, the author explains that it is not for distinguishing body from other things like surface, but to realize the true nature (quiddity) of body. He also addresses an objection based on the Mu'tazilī view of atomic composition. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the author's opening statement about the purpose of the condition.
The author uses a very precise philosophical style.
2
Identify the key distinction
Identify the difference between substance (jawhar) and surface (sath) in terms of dimensional receptivity. How does the author use this to show the condition is not for distinction?
Focus on the argument that surface cannot receive a third dimension at right angles.
3
Understand the Mu'tazilī objection
Read the part about the Mu'tazila position. Why might someone think the condition is needed to exclude surface? Understand the author's response and the phrase 'on the assumption of concession'.
This shows the author's awareness of alternative metaphysical views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا القيد أعني كون تقاطع الأبعاد الثلاثة على زوايا قائمة لم يذكر لتمييز الجسم عن غيره بل لتحقيق ماهيته فإنَّ الجوهر القابل للأبعاد الثلاثة المتقاطعة لا يكون إلا كذلك وهو يمكن فيه أن يكون تقاطعها على الزوايا القائمة والذي يقبل أبعاداً ثلاثة متقاطعة لا على هذا الوجه إنما هو السطح فإنه يمكن أن يفرض فيه بعدان متقاطعان على قوائم ولا يمكن أن يفرض فيه بعد ثالث مقاطع للأولين إلا على حادة ومنفرجة والجوهر لا يتناوله فلا يكون هذا القيد احترازاً عنه كما توهمه بعضهم، واعتذر له بأنَّ المعتزلة ذهبوا إلى أنَّ الجسم مركب من السطوح المركبة من الخطوط المركبة من الجواهر الفردة فيكون السطح عندهم جوهراً، ولما لم يتبين بعد أن الجسم ليس كذلك، وأنَّ السطح يجب أن يكون عرضاً احترز عنه على تقدير التنزل، فتأمل.
And this condition—namely, the intersection of the three dimensions at right angles—was not mentioned to distinguish the body from other things, but to realize its quiddity. Indeed, the substance that is receptive to three intersecting dimensions can only be such that it is possible for their intersection to be at right angles. And that which receives three intersecting dimensions not in this manner is only the surface, for it is possible to assume in it two dimensions intersecting at right angles, but it is not possible to assume in it a third dimension intersecting the first two except at acute and obtuse angles. And the substance does not include it (the surface), so this condition is not a restriction against it, as some have imagined. And an apology was made for it that the Mu'tazila held that the body is composed of surfaces composed of lines composed of atoms, so the surface according to them is a substance. And since it has not yet been established that the body is not like that, and that the surface must be an accident, he restricted it on the assumption of concession. So reflect.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanatory commentary. The author is explaining why the condition that the three dimensions intersect at right angles is included in the definition of body (jism). He begins by stating that this condition is not for distinguishing body from other things (such as surface) but rather for realizing its true quiddity (māhiyya). The reasoning is that a substance (jawhar) that can receive three intersecting dimensions must be such that it allows those dimensions to intersect at right angles. In contrast, a surface can receive two dimensions intersecting at right angles but cannot receive a third dimension intersecting the first two except at oblique angles—acute and obtuse. Since a substance does not include that kind of oblique intersection, the right-angle condition is not needed to exclude surface; surface is already excluded by the fact that a substance does not receive dimensions that intersect obliquely. The author then addresses an objection: some imagined that the condition was meant to exclude surface, and an apology was made for this based on the Mu'tazilī position that a body is composed of surfaces, lines, and atoms, so for them a surface is a substance. The author says that since it has not yet been proven that the body is not composed that way, and that the surface must be an accident, the condition could be considered as a restriction on the assumption of concession. He concludes with 'ta'ammal' (reflect), inviting the reader to ponder the subtlety.

Key Terms
الجسم
الجوهر
السطح
الماهية
القيد
المعتزلة
الجواهر الفردة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The right-angle condition is included in the definition of body specifically to distinguish body from surface.
Correction: The author explicitly states the condition is for realizing quiddity, not for distinction. The distinction follows from the nature of substance and surface.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the condition of right-angled intersection is mentioned primarily for which purpose?
A) To distinguish body from surface
B) To realize the quiddity of body
C) To accommodate the Mu'tazilī view
D) To ensure dimensions are perpendicular

Key Takeaway
The right-angle condition in the definition of body serves to realize the quiddity of body, not merely to distinguish it from surface, although it does that as a consequence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Think of a core belief you hold about Allah's attributes—is it just for 'distinguishing' Islam from other religions, or have you ever sought to realize its quiddity in your heart? What specific step will you take this week to move from distinguishing to realizing?
?
The author mentions the Mu'tazila view as a 'concession' that he does not accept. Where in your own life have you been using a condition or definition as a concession to others while your heart knows the truth? Will you ask Allah tonight to give you the courage to act on the truth, not just accommodate it?
?
This passage ends with 'ta'ammal' (reflect). It is a command, not an invitation. When was the last time you truly reflected on a theological truth until it changed your living? First Doubt: Does the Definition of Body Apply to Hyle?
Author presents and refutes the doubt that the definition applies to hyle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first doubt regarding the definition of body applying to hyle, how it is refuted, and why the definition requires direct assumption of dimensions without intermediary.

Core Idea
The definition of body requires dimensions directly assumable in the substance, not via an intermediary like hyle.

In this passage, the author addresses a critical objection to the definition of body: does it apply to hyle, the underlying substratum? The doubt arises because dimensions can be assumed in hyle through the corporeal form. The refutation clarifies that the definition speaks of direct assumption, not via an intermediary. This lesson guides you through the doubt and its response, sharpening your understanding of how definitions must match their intended objects.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation to get the full argument flow.
Notice the structure: doubt, refutation, objection, answer.
2
Identify the doubt and its basis
Find the statement of the first doubt: the definition applies to hyle because dimensions can be assumed in it through the corporeal form. Note the reasoning: possibility is general with or without intermediary.
The doubt hinges on the phrase 'can be assumed' being taken broadly.
3
Understand the refutation
The author responds that hyle in itself does not allow assumption of dimensions; it only receives the corporeal form, which then receives the dimensions. The definition's wording (fīh) implies direct assumption in the substance itself.
Key point: 'by intermediary' is excluded.
4
Consider the objection and its answer
An objector says: then the definition applies only to the corporeal form, not to the composite body. The author answers that at first glance, the body is precisely that extended substance (the corporeal form), and its subsistence in hyle is not self-evident.
The definition is meant for the commonly understood body.
5
Reflect on the key distinction
Why does 'directness' matter? Reflect on how definitions must capture the essence of the thing without needing intermediary causes. This distinction safeguards the definition from overextension.
This connects to broader principles in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهاهنا شكوك، فعلى مطلق التعريف شكان : الأول : الحد صادق على الهيولى التي هي جزء للجسم المطلق، إذ يمكن فرض الأبعاد المذكورة فيها بواسطة الصورة الجسمية وإمكان فرضها أعم من أن يكون بواسطة أو بغير واسطة. قلنا : ليست الهيولى في حد ذاتها بحيث يمكن فرض الأبعاد فيها بل هي تقبل الصورة الجسمية والصورة الجسمية تقبل الأبعاد المفروضة، والمتبادر من عبارة الحد إمكان فرض الأبعاد نظراً إلى ذات الجوهر فلا يتناول ما يكون بواسطة، فإن قلت : فالحد صادق على الصورة الجسمية وحدها قلنا : لا بأس بذلك لأنَّ الجسم في بادئ الرأي هو هذا الجوهر الممتد في الجهات أعني الصورة الجسمية، وأنَّ هذا الجوهر قائم بجوهر آخر فمما لا يثبت لو ثبت إلا بأنظار دقيقة في أحوال هذا الجوهر الممتد المعلوم وجوده بالضرورة، فالمقصود هاهنا تعريفه. قوله: (ليست الهيولى إلخ) يعني أن الهيولى لا يفرض وذلك الفرض في ذاته لكونها غير متصلة في نفسها. قوله: (بل هي تقبل الصورة إلخ فيكون قبولها لفرض الأبعاد بالفرض كحركة راكب السفينة. قوله: (والمتبادر إلخ فإن كلمة فيه تدل على حصول الفرض المذكور في ذاته لا أن يكون حاصلاً فيما يقارنه سواء كان لذاته أو لأمر آخر فيتناول الحد الجسم، وقوله بواسطة أي في الفرض.
And here there are doubts. On the absolute definition, there are two doubts: The first: the definition applies to the hyle which is a part of the absolute body, because the mentioned dimensions can be assumed in it through the corporeal form, and the possibility of assuming them is more general than being with or without intermediary. We said: The hyle in its own essence is not such that the dimensions can be assumed in it; rather, it receives the corporeal form, and the corporeal form receives the assumed dimensions. And what is understood from the wording of the definition is the possibility of assuming dimensions with respect to the essence of the substance, so it does not include what is by intermediary. If you say: Then the definition applies to the corporeal form alone. We said: There is no harm in that, because the body, at first glance, is this extended substance in the directions, i.e., the corporeal form, and that this substance is subsistent by another substance is not established, if established, except by precise investigations into the states of this extended substance known necessarily to exist. So the purpose here is its definition. His saying: 'The hyle does not...' means that the hyle is not assumed and that assumption in itself because it is not connected in itself. His saying: 'Rather it receives the form...' so its reception of the assumption of dimensions is by assumption, like the movement of a ship's rider. His saying: 'And what is understood...' for the word 'in it' indicates the occurrence of the mentioned assumption in its essence, not that it occurs in what is adjacent to it, whether for itself or for something else, so the definition includes the body. And his saying 'by intermediary' means in the assumption.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage presents the first doubt (shakk) on the definition of body and its refutation. The doubt is that the definition (hadd) holds for hyle (hayūlā) because dimensions can be assumed in it via the corporeal form (ṣūra jismiyya), and the possibility of assumption is general whether with or without an intermediary. The author responds (qulnā) that hyle in itself is not such that dimensions can be assumed; rather, hyle receives the corporeal form, and that form receives the dimensions. The wording of the definition implies the possibility of assuming dimensions directly in the essence of the substance, not through an intermediary. An objection is then considered: if so, the definition applies only to the corporeal form, not to the composite body. The author answers that at first sight, body is precisely this extended substance (jawhar mumtadd) in the directions, i.e., the corporeal form. That this substance is subsistent by another substance (the hyle) is not established without deep investigation, so the definition is correct for the commonly understood body. The subsequent lines are glosses clarifying that hyle does not have connection in itself, and the phrase 'in it' (fīh) indicates that the assumption is directly in the substance, not via something else.

Key Terms
الهيولى
الصورة الجسمية
الحد
الجوهر الممتد
بالواسطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The definition of body can apply to hyle because dimensions can be assumed in it through the corporeal form.
Correction: The definition requires that the substance itself directly allow assumption of dimensions without intermediary. Hyle only allows it through the corporeal form, so the definition does not apply to hyle.

Checkpoint
According to the refutation, why does the definition not apply to hyle?
A) Because hyle cannot receive dimensions even with an intermediary
B) Because the definition requires that the substance itself directly allow assumption of dimensions
C) Because hyle is not a substance
D) Because hyle has no essence

Key Takeaway
The first doubt is refuted by clarifying that the definition requires the possibility of assuming dimensions directly in the substance, not through an intermediary like hyle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

What is one step you can take this week to seek direct understanding of one of His names?
?
The author notes that the composite body (hyle+form) is not the first object of definition. Consider your own faith: Are there beliefs you hold only because you heard them, without personally verifying them from the sources? What is one belief about Allah or the unseen that you have accepted second-hand, and how can you seek direct evidence for it from revelation?
